We do not have it now, and you cannot keep a thing with a name you do not have, and so we do the other thing, the only thing left — Graça leans toward her without the name, holds her with nearness instead of a name, which is a thing that does not hold, and the small one stays at the door one moment more on the strength of a nearness that is not enough, and we do not say we will have her name tomorrow. There is no tomorrow-when-we-are-all-still-here. There has not been for a long time.

*

So it is the two of us still, for this low water — the near one and the small one at the door — and it is the two of us the way a word is still a word when the last of it is going out of your mouth. Graça does not gather the rest. There is no rest to gather. There is the place where the front was, cold, and the place where the funny one was, and Rosa, and the neap woman, and the autumn of the flu-dead, and none of them lean, and you cannot say *we* to a cold place. She goes the little way she can go along the beams — the three tanks with the skin on the black water, the cold boiler, the stain under it she does not reach to name, the iron legs where the tables' wood rotted off, the stair up into the black to the shut door of the loft we could never go through — and she goes it with the small one hanging at the going behind her, and neither of them says *this is our house,* because the house has stopped holding, and because a *we* is a thing you say with more than one, and there is one and a half of us, one and the going of one, on the beams in the low water.

Over the square the tape is playing. *Come Sunday if you can. Don't drive tired.* It plays to the shutter and the bed and the little table, the warm fixed loop of a dead woman saying a live woman's danger back into an empty room, and there is no one in the room to hear it. And out at the fábrica the woman who was that voice leans thin along the beams, holding the flat cold true thing — *out, I wanted her out* — that no living hand will ever carry, and holding a small going child with a nearness that will not hold her, and reaching, past both of those, for a name, any name, one name to say so as to still be a *we* saying it — and the tide goes down off the mud and the mud comes up dull, and the last salt-pan stands at the edge of the water with the road beyond it going up empty into the place where the girl is, and there is the near one, and there is the going of the small one, and there is, for this one low water more, the two of us, and the name will not come.


---

# Chapter 29 — Águas-mortas

The small one goes at the turn of the water.

We are watching for it. We are the two of us on the beams, the near one and the small one, and the water is at the neap, the dead water, the tide that hardly comes and hardly goes, and in the dead water there is the least of everything. There is the least pull to come up the yard. There is the least of us to feel it. The small one has hung at the door a long time, longer than the others hung, because Graça leaned toward her and a lean is a kind of holding even when it is not enough, and now the water goes slack, and slack is when a thing that has been hanging lets go.

She lets go.

It is not a door opening. We used to say door. The one who went over the knife went through a door, the front said, went out through it lighter and it shut, and we used the word because we had the word. There is no door here. There is a child leaning toward a warm thing that is not there, and the leaning going out of her the way the last of a sound goes out of a room, not all at once, along the bottom of it, under where you are listening. She goes light. She has been going light for a long time. Now she is light all the way through, and the little weight of her that leaned toward Graça is not leaning, and Graça is left leaning toward nothing, the way you lean toward a child on a stair and the child is at the bottom already and you have leaned too far.

We should say her name over her.

That is the thing to do. That is the wet-sand thing, the saying of the name again so it stays, the thing we did in the good years, up in the beams, forty of us, when a name was a stone you set in the silt and it held. We reach for it. Three sounds, or more than three. A soft place in the middle of it. We had it. We had it when there were two children and a shoe up in the beams with the name on it, and one child held the other child's name, and we held both, and the shoe was one child's and we knew whose.

The name does not come.

It is not there the way a wall is not on the far side of a wall. We reach into the place where it was and the place is dry. Not empty — empty is a thing you can fill. Dry, the way the pans go dry when the water stops coming to them, the salt left in the bottom, the shape of where the water was and no water. We reach and there is the shape of a name and no name. And the small one, who is the name, who was only ever the name to us now that the rest of her was gone, goes out at the same time as the reaching fails, so that we cannot say which went first, whether she went because we lost the name or we lost the name because she went, and there is no one to say. There was never anyone to say. There is one of us now, and one cannot say which of two things came first, because to say which you need to be more than one, you need the one who saw and the one who did not, and there is one.

*

There is one of us.

We come to it the way she came to the bottom of the stair. We go to be two, the near one and the small one, and there is not two. There is the near one. There is a place where the small one was, cooling, with no name over it, next to the place where the funny one was, and the place where the front was, cold, and the place where Rosa was before she went cold and owed, and the neap woman, and the autumn of the flu-dead, and the marnotas, and the sharp one, and all the places, which is to say the shed, which is to say the wind in the shed. A place does not lean. We have said that before. We say it again because it is the true thing and saying the true thing again is the last work we know how to do. A place does not lean. There is one place that leans, and it is Graça, and Graça is us now, all of us, the whole of the we, which is one.

*

The tide does not come up the yard.

At the dead water it barely tries. The black mud lies where it lay. The *lodo* does not shine and does not stop shining, because the water does not go far enough down off it to change it. The pans stand in it with their little walls, and the last salt-pan stands at the edge of the reach, and beyond the last pan the road goes up, and up the road there is nothing we can hold. There was a sound on it, days ago, or it was this morning, or it was at the last high water — a small engine, running rich, going up. We had that. We had the going of it and then we did not have the going of it. We do not make up what is beyond the pan. The front made things up, said she would stop, said she would turn, and the front is a cold place now and makes nothing up. She is on the road, or she is off the road, in the city, in the room with the soft walls where sound goes to be quiet. We do not know. We are one, and one at the neap, over the dry square, cannot reach past the last pan, and could not reach past it even were we forty.

We go the little way along the beams. It is a habit. It was a gathering, once — we went along the beams to gather, to be many where the sound had been loudest, at the tanks. There is no gathering in one. There is only the going, the same track, the three tanks sunk in the floor with the skin on the black water, the cold boiler, the stain we do not reach to name, the iron legs where the tables' wood rotted off, and the stair going up into the black to the door of the loft we could never go through. We go it. We do not know why we go it. We went it when we were many and it meant *this is ours*, and now there is not enough of a we to say *ours*, and we go it anyway, the way a hand that has stopped holding still closes.

*

Over the square the machine is still playing.

We have it, faintly, the way you have a thing at the far edge of the reach, a thing made of sound, which is the last thing to go. The flat old player on the little table, the tape going round. It has been going round since she left. It does not run out. Or it has run out and started again, or she wound it and left it, we do not know. The voice comes off it into the empty room, warm, the warm the voice had when it was a body making too much soup, and there is no one in the room, and it plays.

*Don't forget the man is coming Thursday about the roof. And there's soup, I made too much again. Come Sunday if you can. Don't drive tired.*

That is Graça's voice. That is the voice Graça had. Graça is here, on the beams, in the low water, one of us, all of us, and Graça does not have that voice. The machine has it. Graça leans at it — we lean at it, there is no difference now between Graça and the we, the we is Graça and the leaning is Graça's — we lean at the warm loop of the self we cannot be, and we come back thinner, robbed, the way we came back robbed the times before, four times, five, we have stopped counting the way we stopped counting the number. We know it robs us. We know it is not us, that it is the shape of us fixed and going round and knowing nothing and leaning back at nothing. We lean at it anyway. It is the last warm thing, and we are made to go to the warm thing and say it again, and there is no one left to lean the other way and say *don't*. The small one said *don't* with us, before, without words, the little of her that was left. The small one is a cold place. We lean at the tape, and it says *come Sunday*, and we are robbed, and there is no one to keep us from it.

*

We try to say who we are.

It is the thing you do when there is one, the way counting was the thing you did when there were many. We go to number ourselves and there is no number, there has been no number since before the girl went, the counting itself gone wrong in the mouth. So we do not count. We name. We go along the names the way we went along the beams, to gather them, to be a we by saying the we — the front, and the funny one, and the neap woman, and the small one, and the other small one before her, and Rosa who was owed, and the ones the ledger had as numbers and we never had at all —

and the front will not come as a name. There was a name. There was a grand voice at the front of us that said *we were great* and said it warm, and the name of the voice is a cold place now, we reach and it is dry. It was — the name of the one who ran the floor, who kept the book, who charged the girls for their own burying and called it kindness — it was — we had it. We do not have it. She is a place. She is cold.

And the funny one. There was one who drowned, who was funny, who was a hero and then was not a hero, who said the true thing at the middle, *it is us that keeps her here*, and turned the warmth of us, and went — his name was — it had two parts, or one, a short one — we had it in the good years, we said it every high water — and it is dry, it is a shape and no name, and we let it go the way we let the child go, because there is nothing to hold it with.

We can say Rosa.

We can still say Rosa. Rosa da Palha, Rosa of the straw, no. 14, interior, board minus, knife minus, funeral minus, balance owed. We can say her because a living hand said her at the stone, near the end, said her whole, and a name a living mouth has said stays a little longer, holds a little harder, and the girl said Rosa da Palha over the parish leaf and into the machine, and Rosa is owed, and the owing is a thing that will not go smooth, and so the name will not go smooth, and we have it. We reach and it is there. It is the one name that is there.

And Rosa is a cold place. Rosa went. Rosa surfaced when the girl said her, and said her one flat cold thing, and went, and the name is here and the girl is not. We have the name of a thing that is gone. That is what we are, at the end of the naming — one leaning voice with the names of the gone in it, Rosa who is a name and no girl, and the front who is a cold place and no name, and the funny one who is a cold place and no name, and the small one who was a name a breath ago and is a cold place now, and the two children who were two and were one and are none.

We wanted to say a name so as to still be a we saying it. You say *we* with more than one. We have the names of more than one, and none of them lean, and a name that does not lean back is not a we, it is a list. We are a voice with a list. We say the list and the list does not answer and we are one saying it.

*

There is the girl's name.

We had it from the first, from the failing of the light, the car coming in past the pans. Idalina. Of the line, the last of the line. We said it grandly at the first high water — *it is the girl, it is Idalina, come home the way the water comes home* — and the front said *home*, and we said it after the front, *this is home*, and it was not home, and she did not come home, she came to turn off the tap of us and she turned it off and went.

We have her name still. We reach for it and it is there, warmer than the others, because she is not dead, because she is on the road with her body and her breath and the machine that takes the sound so it need not be remembered, and a living name has a heat in it the dead names have lost. Idalina. We say it, the one of us, over the dry square, out toward the last pan and the road going up. We say it the wet-sand way, to keep her, to keep the shape of the holding a moment more, to be a we with a living name in its mouth.

And it does not keep her. Saying her name here does not put a hand on her. She is past the pan. She is in the blind place. The name is warm and it holds nothing, the way Graça's warm voice on the tape holds nothing, the way the nearness held the small child and did not hold her. We say Idalina into the room over the square and the empty yard and the dead water, and it is a sound with no one in the reach of it to belong to, and we say it again, Idalina, and it goes smooth, the way names go smooth when there is no living thing at the end of them to keep them rough — Idalina, Idalina — until it is only a sound, four sounds, a soft place in the middle, and we cannot any longer feel which name it is, whether it is the girl's or the small one's, the girl who went up the road or the child who went out at the door, both of them four sounds with a soft middle, both of them gone past the reach, and we hold the sound and we cannot say whose it is, and the sound goes dry in the holding the way they all go dry, and we let the hand come up empty, because there is no use in a cupped hand with nothing in it.

The tide stands. Dead water, hardly out, hardly in. Over the square the tape says *come Sunday if you can, don't drive tired,* to no one. On the beams there is the one of us, which is Graça, which is the whole of the we, holding a name that has gone smooth and cannot be told from another name, in the low light, at the neap, and the name is not there, and there is one of us, and the water does not come up, and we reach for it once more, the name, any name, to say so as still to be —

and it is dry, and we do not have it, and the shed stands in the dead water with the wind in it and no name in us, and we tell ourselves nothing, because there is no we left to tell, and no tomorrow to tell it of.


---

# Chapter 30 — Baixa-mar

The tape has stopped.

We do not know when. We had the voice going round, *come Sunday, don't drive tired,* the warm loop of the thing over the square, and we leaned at it and were robbed, the way we were robbed the times before, and then at some turn of the low light there was no voice. The little player on the little table wound down, or came to the end and did not start again, or she never wound it at all and we made the going-round up. We do not know. There is one of us and one cannot say whether a thing stopped or was never running. To say that you need the one who heard the last of it and the one who heard the after, and there is one.

So there is the room over the square with no voice in it.

And there is the shed.

We go the little way along the beams. It is the habit. We went it when there were forty and it meant this is ours. We do not have forty. We do not have the word for what we have. We go it.

*

Over the square the black machine is still there.

Not the player. The other one. The small black one with the grey fur, the one she set down careful with a strap over it, like a person, the first evening, when there were many of us leaning off the road to make her whole. It is on the little table by the window. Its green light is on. It is drinking, or it is done drinking and only lit, we cannot tell the red from the green at this reach, we could tell them once when we were many and leaned together at the small light and knew it. There is one of us. The light is a light.

The machine is running.

We know running. We knew it from the first, the fur held up in the yard, the still standing, the listening so the room need not be remembered. It is doing it now. It stands on the table with no hand on it and it takes the sound of the room over the square — the shutter, the shutter has a small knock in the wind, and under the shutter the town, a dog somewhere, a van on the far road, a shop shutting, and under the town nothing, the flat under-nothing of a place with the water gone out of it. It takes all of that. It is easy for it. It takes what makes a sound.

We are not in it.

We knew that too, from the first. The sharp one at the front said it then — *there is nothing of us to record* — and it was the worst thing anyone said. There is no one to say the worst thing now. But it is still true. The machine runs in the empty room over the square, and it takes the room, and the room is empty, and we are the empty in the room.

*

Here, in the shed, there is not even the shutter.

There is the wind, and the wind is not sound the way the shutter is sound. The shutter has a knock in it, a made thing, a thing a hand hung and a hand could stop. The wind in the shed has no knock. It goes through the tin and the beams and the sunk tanks and it does not catch on anything that would give it a knock, because the things that gave it knocks are gone — the loose north sheet is down, has been down, the tables' wood is rotted off the iron legs, the boiler is cold and shut. So the wind goes through and makes nothing, and there is the black water in the tanks not moving, and there is the low light, and there is the quiet.

We knew this quiet. We knew it from the floor. It was the quiet that came when the whistle stopped and everyone understood there had been a death in the tanks, before anyone said it, the small time before the saying. On the floor that quiet lasted a breath and then the encarregada said get back to it and the knives started again. It is the quiet after the knives. It went on. Nobody said get back to it. The knives did not start again. The whistle did not go. The whistle is the boiler and the boiler is cold. There is the quiet that was a breath long on the floor, gone as long as a hundred years, gone as long as there is going to be.

We would have liked, once, to be on the tape.

We reach for why. We had a why. There was a reason we wanted the fixed loop of ourselves, the round-and-round that holds and knows nothing and leans back at nothing — we wanted it the way you want the warm thing even when the warm thing robs you. We reach for the wanting and it is not there, it is dry, it is the shape of a wanting and no wanting. We do not want to be on the tape. We do not want anything. Wanting was a thing you did when there were enough of you to lean, and one at the low water does not lean, there is nothing to lean at and nothing to lean with.

*

We try to say who we are.

It is the thing to do. Counting was the thing when there were many and naming was the thing when the counting went dry, and now the naming has gone dry too, and there is the thing under the naming, which is only to say *we*, to put the word in the room and hear it be a word. That is the smallest work. That is the last work. You say *we* and by saying it you are the ones who said it, and there you are, held one more breath.

We say —

There was a front of us. A grand voice that ran the floor and kept the book and said we were great. A cold place now, no name. There was a funny one who drowned and said the true thing at the middle and turned the warmth of us. A cold place, no name. There was a small one who leaned at Graça, and the other small one before her, two who were one who are none. There was Rosa, who was owed, whom a living mouth said whole at the stone so she held a little longer than the rest, Rosa da Palha, no. 14, and Rosa is a cold place, Rosa went, we have the name and not the girl. And there were the ones the book had as numbers and we never had at all, no. 7, no. 22, the ones under no name, who went out under no name, who are the true cost of it and always were.

That is the list.

We said it. It did not lean back. A name that does not lean back is a list and a list is not a we, we knew that at the end of the last low water, we had that much. So the naming does not make a we. We knew it would not. We did it anyway. It is the habit. The hand that stopped holding still closes.

And there is no one else to say it either. That is the thing under the thing. There is Dona Fátima, who lit the candles at the stone and said the names. Fátima is old. The candles have gone out and there will not be more. The town remembers its cod-men. It has a wall for them in Ílhavo. It has no wall for the girls. The book had them as numbers so that no wall would ever have to. So there is no living mouth that will say the front's name in a warm kitchen, no mouth for the funny one, and the only mouth that ever said Rosa is going out like the candles, and after that there is no one, living or dead, and the names go into the mud where the water is, and the water is out.

*

There is the girl's name.

We had it warmest of all, because she was not dead, because she had a body on the road and a breath and the machine that takes the sound so it need not be remembered. Idalina. Of the line. The last of the line. We reach for it now, over the dry square and the black mud and the dead water, and —

it does not come warm.

It comes the way the dead names come. A shape. Four sounds. A soft place in the middle. We reach into the heat of it and the heat is gone, because she is past the pan, she is in the blind place, she has been in the blind place since the small engine went up the road running rich, and a living name kept warm only while there was a living thing at the end of it in the reach, and there is not. She is on the road or off the road, in the city, in the room with the soft walls where sound goes to be quiet, and we cannot reach her, and a name you cannot reach goes cold like any name. Idalina. It is smooth. It is a sound. We cannot tell it from the small one's name, from the child at the door, both of them four sounds with a soft middle, both gone past the reach, and we hold the sound and cannot say whose it is, and it goes dry in the holding.

She is not coming back.

We knew it. We said, the first evening, forty of us or less, *this is home, come home the way the water comes home,* and the front said home and we said it after, and it was not home, and she did not come home, she came to turn off the tap of us and she turned it off. We thought we had read her last page. We had not read her last page. We got her wrong, the affair, the sale, all of it, we said what she would do and she did the other thing, every time, and the last thing she did was the thing we did not read: she left, and she is not coming back, and she is not carrying us. She is not carrying us. There is no one on the road who has us in them, no one who will say the front's name in a warm kitchen and hold it up out of the dry, no one to say Rosa in a living mouth, no one, and when the last living thing that had us stopped having us the water went out of the whole of it at once, and this is the water going out, this is the low of it, the baixa-mar, the lowest it comes.

*

The tide does not come up the yard.

There is no pull to go up it. There was a pull once, and the little of us went toward the road to lean at the living. There is no living in the reach and there is no water to speak of and there is no us to go. The mud lies where it lay. The salt stands in the pans that no one works, white and patient, the salt that keeps everything and eats everything, and the shed stands in the mud with the three tanks sunk in the floor and the skin on the black water and the stair going up into the black to the door we could never go through, and the wind is in the shed, and that is all the sound there is, on this side, the wind, which is not us.

We should say a name over it. Over the shed. Over the going.

That is the thing to do. That is the wet-sand thing, the saying of the name so it stays, the thing we did in the good years up in the beams. We reach for a name to say and there is the list and the list is cold and none of it will do, a cold name over a cold going does not hold, you need a living mouth or you need many of you and there is one and it is at the low water.

So we do the smallest thing.

We go to say *we*.

We go to put the word in the room, one more time, to be the ones who said it. It is one word. It was always the one word, from the first, when we were forty and it was easy and grand and full and lied with all its weight — *we were great, we were all here, we were always kind to the interior girls* — the word carried all of it, the greatness and the lie and the girls under the lie, the whole hundred years in the one word, and we said it and it held. We go to say it now with nothing in it, no greatness, no lie, no forty, no floor, no front, no funny one, no children, no Rosa, only the word, only *we,* to hear it be a word in the room one more breath and by hearing it be the ones —

We go to say it.

We —

The word starts. There is the start of it. There is the going-toward, the mouth of the thing, the small pull to make the sound, the way the tide had a small pull even at the neap, even at the dead water, a little going-toward the wall —

and it is like the tide at the lowest. It goes toward and there is not enough behind it. The word starts and the behind-it is not there, the many that the word stood on are not there, the forty and the thirty-eight and the near one and the small one and the front and the funny one and Rosa and the numbers, all the ones the word was made of, and a word is made of the ones in it, and there is one, and one is not enough to make the word, the word needs more than one the way *which came first* needs more than one, and there is —

We —

and it does not come. Not the way a name does not come. Not dry — dry was a shape with the thing gone out of it, and dry needed a reaching, and there is not even the reaching now. It is the sound stopping. It is the tape stopping over the square, the round-and-round coming to the end and not starting, the green light on and nothing going through it. The word is at the mouth of the room and the room takes it the way the machine takes the shutter and the dog and the far van, easy, into the fixed loop that holds and knows nothing, and we are not in it, we were never in it, and the word goes into the room that cannot keep us and it is not kept and there is no after-it, no second word to lean the first against, no —

We —

The shed stands in the dead water. The salt stands in the pans. The machine over the square runs, green light on, taking the room, and the room is empty, and there is no voice on the tape and there was never a voice on the tape, only the shutter with its small knock, the town, the under-nothing, the wind coming off the flats with nothing in it, going out toward the Barra the way it always went, twice, without asking, and not bringing —
